This design for Megalon is so weirdly haunting in a VERY good way. He looks like a monster being unleashed to destroy everything and wreak havoc, but he ACTS like a warrior that was given a mission to destroy anything that could threaten his kingdom. He's like a master martial artist that wastes no effort and develops new techniques as the fight unfolds, becoming an escalating threat in the heat of battle. His father, by comparison, is a savage brawler who is all fury and violence and no finesse. jr. is different, jr. is slow, steady, and skilled as all hell. He's a legitimate master fighter, and that combined with the raw power and godlike endurance of his father is a truly frightening combo because he rarely will ever panic and expend too much energy, and he has a LOT of energy to use up. He's a walking mountain of doom with the skill of akuma from street fighter. a terrifying monster indeed.

What I liked: The amount of work put into this shows. It looks good.  Remembering Megalons seatopian origin is cool. Megalons new design was great, and his hydraulic drills and spikes were neat changes.  What i didn't like: Megalon felt like he had no personality compared to his original, and he died, instead of surviving.  None of Megalon;s attacks felt like they did anything at all except for his spike bombs, and the suicide charge. The fact that the older megalon fought for way longer and survived vs this short fight and dying still makes it feel like showa Megalon is stronger despite the obvious glow up. I know Godzilla is an absolute unit but him immediately countering everything felt cheap. He displayed abilities that should have been used against gigan rex but weren't and didn't feel like he needed these new abilities to win this fight.

Very nicely done. Lovely animation. Love that these shorts that seem to be from the same people that gave us Gigan Rex are taking some of  Gojis older foes, and giving them a fresh new spin. Not too sure about Godzillas design in this, will have to study it more, but Megalon looks great! A fresh take on an old Kaiju, giving him some new moves and making him look pretty terrifying all things considered. And seeing as this takes place some time after Gigan Rex (which takes place after Godzilla vs Destroyah), I actually really love the idea of Godzilla Jr. having the ability to use his atomic energy in new ways. Like the short burst from the spins propelling him (btw, love love LOVE that callback to OG Gojis iconic kick against Megalon, fricking badass dude!), to him concentrating it into his arms for small Atomic Punches and even firing beams from his hands. Like how has no one done that with him before? And the fact that they gave to Jr. helps him stand out more from his dad. Like that Jr. somehow has better control over his atomic energy than his father. All in all, fantastic short! Bravo to all involved. <3

been waiting all year. this was absolutly worth it you love to see kaiju who didnt get much spotlight back in the day get a much needed refresher
This did not disappoint! I liked how human perspectives were added - "vs. Gigan Rex", as amazing as that was, felt a little empty without the pedestrians. This short feels like its actually part of the world rather than just a setting for kaiju fights.  The glow-up to Megalon was magnificent, as well as the modern rendition of his abilities. This managed to overcome the original suit's campiness while still keeping it recognizable. Godzilla looks as great as he did last year. I love the new abilities he depicted. It's funny; I had actually conceived a sort of "atomic punch/claw swipe" in a version of how I might do G, and to see it in action was awesome! And I had hoped this would have a version of the infamous flying-kick, but was worried it would break the more grounded/serious tone of this short. How it was depicted here managed to keep the hilarity while not breaking the tone (I actually had to pause and rewind at that moment just because I wasn't expecting it to be shown as such; it brought me such joy to see it preserved).  Absolutely incredible work! It's great we're getting a sort of mini-series like this.
